<script>
	function goToTopic(topic) {
		var topicMap = applySpecialCharacterMapping(topic); 
		var url = "/xpl/topicbrowse.jsp?topic=" + escape(topicMap);
		window.top.location.href = url;
	}
</script>

		<!-- ngIf: ::vm.details.impactStatement || vm.details.abstract || vm.details.scope || vm.details.purpose  || vm.details.previewImage --><div ng-if="::vm.details.impactStatement || vm.details.abstract || vm.details.scope || vm.details.purpose  || vm.details.previewImage" ng-class="vm.details.graphicalAbstract ? 			<!-- ngIf: ::vm.details.abstract --><div ng-if="::vm.details.abstract" class="ng-scope">
				<strong>Abstract:</strong>
				<div class="abstract-text ng-binding" ng-bind-html="::vm.details.abstract">The performance of an RF identification (RFID) system can be limited by the static radiation pattern of a reader or interrogator. In this paper, a novel and low-power CMOS chip has been designed to enable beam steering for the RFID interrogator. This is suitable for the RFID system, operating from 900-MHz to 2.4-GHz bands, which uses passive and active RF tags. Our solution does not change the basic transceiver design in order to minimize the cost of the system. The chip has been implemented in 130-nm CMOS. It can provide up to eight time shifted signals to feed the multiple RF synthesizers in a phased array. This is suitable for the RFID reader, which requires multibands and multimodes, covering ISO-18000-6, Electronic Product Code, and IEEE 802.11b/g standards. The size of this die is 1.2 mm<sup>2</sup> and it consumes only 10 mA. It can provide multiple delayed signals with 5-ps resolution. This will translate to a 2deg scanned angle at 2.4-GHz band. Measured results for the integrated circuit and phased arrays will be provided.</div>
			</div><!-- end ngIf: ::vm.details.abstract -->			
			<!-- ngIf: ::vm.details.scope -->

<div id="BodyWrapper" class="ArticlePage" xmlns:ieee="http://www.ieeexplore.ieee.org"><div id="article">
<div class="section" id="sec1"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION I.</div><h2>Introduction</h2></div><p>The number of RF identification (RFID) applications has increased rapidly in recent years. These are primarily driven by the demands from the major customers such as Walmart <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref1" id="context_ref_1_1">[1]</a>, the Department of Defence, etc., and the emerging international standards from the International Standards Organization (ISO), Electronic Product Code (EPC), and IEEE. These applications can be highly diversified. Typically, users who require short range (0.5–10 m) tracking exploit passive RF tags. These are interrogated by a reader operating at 800/900-MHz bands, which comply with EPC and ISO standards. Here, the key concern is to power up the passive tags. The dc power supply of the tags comes from the external RF power radiated by the RFID reader. The performance in this system is primarily limited by the national spectrum regulations and the static antenna beam pattern. Users who require tracking items over longer distances (up to a few hundreds of meters), prefer RFID readers or access points operating at 2.4 GHz. Typically these are using WIFI-IEEE 802.11b/g or ZigBee-IEEE 802.15.4 standards to locate battery-powered tags. RFID reader that use beam steering <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref2" id="context_ref_2_1">[2]</a>–<a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref3" id="context_ref_3_1">[3]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref4" id="context_ref_4_1">[4]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref5" id="context_ref_5_1">[5]</a> can improve the system performance.</p><p>Emerging RFID applications are driving the need for multiple modes and frequency bands. Hence, a beam-steering technique, which can enable multiband and multimode transceivers to operate at 900 MHz and 2.4 GHz, is highly desirable.</p><p>In this paper, we will present the design of a novel beam-steering integrated circuit (IC) to control the phases of the frequency synthesizers (FSs) <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref4" id="context_ref_4_1">[4]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref5" id="context_ref_5_1">[5]</a> in a phased array. This method is suitable for a multiband and multimode RFID interrogator or reader operating from 900 MHz to 2.4 GHz. Our beam-steering method has exploited the concept of analog delay-locked loop (DLL) <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref6" id="context_ref_6_1">[6]</a>. We have implemented this on 130-nm CMOS to give variable time shifted signals up to 5-ps resolution. The radiation patterns of our phased arrays at 900 MHz and 2.4 GHz will be measured to validate the performance. Finally, the chip was also tested with a phased-array reader to boost the reading rates of the passive RFID tags in a cluttered indoor environment. This electronic beam-steering IC was able to achieve picosecond precision to enable fine beam scanning from 900-MHz to 2.4-GHz bands. The system design of the beam-steering array will be discussed in <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec2" class="fulltext-link">Section II</a>. We will reveal the IC architecture design for the beam-steering device in <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec3" class="fulltext-link">Section III</a> and present the measured results in <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec4" class="fulltext-link">Section IV</a>. Finally, our conclusions are summarized in <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec5" class="fulltext-link">Section V</a>.</p></div>
<div class="section" id="sec2"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION II.</div><h2>System Design of Phased Array</h2></div><div class="section_2" id="sec2a"><h3>A. width: 0px; height: 4.002em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.002em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; position: absolute; width: 1.302em; right: 0.003em;"><span class="mtd" id="mjx-eqn-${\hbox{(3)}}$"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-135"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-136"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-137"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-138"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-139"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-140"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-141"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-142" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">(3)</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.002em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.002em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.997em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 2.628em;"></span></span></nobr></span></div><script type="math/tex; mode=display" id="MathJax-Element-10">\tau={\varphi\over 2\pi f}.\eqno{\hbox{(3)}}</script></tex-math><span class="formula"><span class="link">View Source</span><img aria-describedby="qtip-0" style="display:inline;" title="Right-click on figure or equation for MathML and additional features." data-hasqtip="0" class="qtooltip moreInfo" alt="Right-click on figure for MathML and additional features." src="/assets/img/icon.support.gif" border="0" height="20" width="24" /><span class="tex tex2jax_ignore" style="display:none;">\tau={\varphi\over 2\pi f}.\eqno{\hbox{(3)}}</span></span></disp-formula>Beam forming can be designed using analog and digital techniques <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref2" id="context_ref_2_2a">[2]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref3" id="context_ref_3_2a">[3]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref8" id="context_ref_8_2a">[8]</a>, and <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref9" id="context_ref_9_2a">[9]</a>, but there is a tradeoff in performance <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref5" id="context_ref_5_2a">[5]</a>. It is important to achieve low power and low cost in a commercial RFID system. Our earlier works have used a dual port direct digital synthesizer (DDS) to provide reference signals with small time delay to drive the phased-locked loops (PLLs) in the transmitters for a phased array <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref4" id="context_ref_4_2a">[4]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref5" id="context_ref_5_2a">[5]</a> operating at 800–900 MHz. However, the architecture of a typical DDS is meant for generating signals with variable frequency and phase. It requires complex and high-speed digital processing and high-performance digital-to-analog converter to produce analog waveforms. Generally, DDS requires high power since it consumes hundreds of milliwatts. Hence, we have proposed a new time-delay chip for the steering RF beam. It only consumes 10 mA, much lower power than DDS and the CMOS die size is only 1.2 <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-11-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-156" role="math" style="width: 2.652em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.103em; height: 0px; font-size: 125%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.302em 1002.1em 2.452em -999.998em); top: -2.298em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-157"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-158"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.103em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.402em 1001.65em 4.152em -999.998em); top: -3.998em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-159"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-160"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-161"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-162"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-163" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">mm</span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.002em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -4.348em; left: 1.652em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-164"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-165"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-166" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">2</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.002em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.302em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.059em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.191em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-11">{\hbox{mm}}^{2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. This will lead to a low-cost solutions for RFID applications <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref6" id="context_ref_6_2a">[6]</a>. Our designs provide the reference clocks or signals for each PLL within the RF transmitter and receiver, as shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig1" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 1</a> so it does not require any modification to these transceivers <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref3" id="context_ref_3_2a">[3]</a>. It can achieve a fine degree of scanning by exploiting time shifts in picoseconds. The chip will drive the RF synthesizers for the transmitters and receivers so as to steer the radiated beam adaptively. 5-ps delay will translate to about 4.65° scanned at 2.4 GHz. This performance can easily match the high resolution obtained from a digital beam-forming array.</p><p>A typical PLL used in an RFID transceiver includes a phase frequency detector (PFD) and charge pump (CP), loop filter (LF), voltage-controlled oscillator (VCO), integer, or fractional divider <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-12-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-167" role="math" style="width: 1.153em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.903em; height: 0px; font-size: 125%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.453em 1000.9em 2.452em -999.998em); top: -2.298em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-168"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-169" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">N<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.102em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.302em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.059em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.003em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-12">N</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, as shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig2" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 2</a>. The transfer function can be represented in the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-13-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-170" role="math" style="width: 0.603em; </p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig2"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4808169/4808169-fig-2-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4808169/4808169-fig-2-small.gif" alt="Figure 2" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 2. </b><fig><p>Typical FS includes CP-PFD LPF, VCO, and integer-<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-15-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-283" role="math" style="width: 1.153em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.003em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-16">N</script></tex-math></inline-formula> for PLL.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/4808169/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div> The source signal <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-17-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-289" role="math" style="width: 2.152em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.702em; height: 0px; font-size: 125%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.403em 1001.6em 2.702em -999.998em); top: -2.298em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-290"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-291" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">x</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-292" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">(</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-293" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">t</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-294" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">)</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.302em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.372em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.378em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-17">x(t)</script></tex-math></inline-formula> triggers a change in phase <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-18-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-295" role="math" style="width: 1.652em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.302em; height: 0px; font-size: 125%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.702em 1001.3em 2.652em -999.998em); top: -2.298em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-296"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-297"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.302em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.402em 1000.6em 4.353em -999.998em); top: -3.998em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-298" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">φ</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.002em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.848em; left: 0.653em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-299"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-300"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-301" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">i</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-302" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">n</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.002em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.302em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.309em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.941em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-18">\varphi_{\rm in}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> (e.g., a step phase or ramp phase) at the input of a PLL in the transceiver. The output signal of the PLL will change with the phase accordingly and settle at <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-19-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-303" role="math" style="width: 2.202em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.752em; height: 0px; font-size: 125%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.702em 1001.75em 2.652em -999.998em); top: -2.298em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-304"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-305"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.752em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.402em 1000.6em 4.353em -999.998em); top: -3.998em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-306" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">φ</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.002em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.848em; left: 0.653em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-307"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-308"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-309" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">o</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-310" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">u</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-311" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">t</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.002em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.302em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.309em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.941em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-19">\varphi_{\rm out}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> in the steady state <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref10" id="context_ref_10_2a">[10]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref11" id="context_ref_11_2a">[11]</a>. In our case, the source signal for the PLL is derived from our beam-steering device. It provides multiple signals with variable time shift or delay. This delay will translate to phase change for each transceiver in the array in order to steer the RF beam. The data source may create in-phase (I) and/or quadrature (Q) signal, which is used to modulate the carrier, as shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig1" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 1</a>. Alternatively, data can be modulated on the carrier by switching the power amplifier (PA) <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref5" id="context_ref_5_2a">[5]</a>. The output of each PA is finally connected to the antenna. The outputs between two antennas in the array produce a phase difference of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-20-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-312" role="math" style="width: 2.202em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.752em; height: 0px; font-size: 125%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.702em 1001.75em 2.652em -999.998em); top: -2.298em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-313"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-314"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.752em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.402em 1000.6em 4.353em -999.998em); top: -3.998em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-315" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">φ</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.002em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.848em; left: 0.653em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-316"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-317"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-318" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">o</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-319" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">u</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-320" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">t</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.002em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.302em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.309em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.941em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-20">\varphi_{\rm out}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, which is ultimately summed together in the air, but in the receiving mode, each chain will down-convert the RF signal to IF. This is then added or summed using an analog combiner at the IF. In this paper, only beam steering for the transmitter chains operating at 900-MHz and 2.4-GHz bands using this time-delay IC module will be evaluated.<p></p></div></div>
<div class="section" id="sec3"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION III.</div><h2>Beam-Steering IC Designs</h2></div><p>A true time-delay circuit can be realized as a passive transmission lines or resistive (R) and capacitive (C) components at the expense of a large silicon die area <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref12" id="context_ref_12_3">[12]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref13" id="context_ref_13_3">[13]</a> and high losses in power. In addition, the timing accuracy may suffer due to process variations. Alternatively, active circuits can be used to produce time-delayed signals <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref12" id="context_ref_12_3">[12]</a>–<a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref13" id="context_ref_13_3">[13]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref14" id="context_ref_14_3">[14]</a>, which occupy a smaller die area, but it is not easy to achieve a small time delay, in the order of picoseconds, typically found in a DDS. Moreover, the DDS consumes higher power and requires a large silicon area, which leads to higher cost <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref15" id="context_ref_15_3">[15]</a>. A commercial DDS typically consumes a few hundred milliamperes. Several DDSs or a DDS with multiple outputs are required for a phased array. This leads to even higher power consumption and cost. Our electronic beam-steering device, which exploits true time-delay outputs using active CMOS circuits <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref6" id="context_ref_6_3">[6]</a>, aims to provide a better and alternative solution to this problem.</p><p>The principle of our time-delay circuits is based on analog DLL. DLLs are widely used to generate on-chip clocks in microprocessors, memory interfaces, and communication ICs. The design offers good performance in the timing jitter as compared to the conventional PLL <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref16" id="context_ref_16_3">[16]</a>. The jitter does not accumulate, as there is no close-loop in the delay cells. A basic DLL, as shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig3" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 3</a>, consists of a series of voltage-controlled delay cells that forms the voltage control delay line (VCDL), a phase detector (PD), a CP and an LF. A PD instead of a PFD is often required in a DLL as the output clock needs only one cycle delay of the input reference signal <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-21-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-321" role="math" style="width: 2.902em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.302em; height: 0px; font-size: 125%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.403em 1002.2em 2.702em -999.998em); top: -2.298em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-322"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-323" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">(</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-324"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.502em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.152em 1000.75em 4.152em -999.998em); top: -3.998em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-325"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-326"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-327" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">V<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.202em;"></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.002em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.848em; left: 0.603em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-328"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-329"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-330" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">r</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-331" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">e</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-332" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">f<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.053em;"></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.002em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-333" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">)</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.302em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.372em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.378em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-21">({V}_{\rm ref})</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. A PD ensures that the output signal <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-22-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-334" role="math" style="width: 3.902em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 3.103em; height: 0px; font-size: 125%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.403em 1003em 2.752em -999.998em); top: -2.298em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-335"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-336" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">(</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-337"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.302em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.152em 1000.75em 4.152em -999.998em); top: -3.998em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-338"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-339"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-340" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">V<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.202em;"></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.002em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.848em; left: 0.603em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-341"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-342"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-343" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">d</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-344" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">e</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-345" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">l</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-346" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">a</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-347" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">y</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.002em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-348" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">)</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.302em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.434em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.441em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-22">({V}_{\rm delay})</script></tex-math></inline-formula> will not lock to the harmonics (multiple cycles) of the input clock.</p><p>
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig3"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4808169/4808169-fig-3-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4808169/4808169-fig-3-small.gif" alt="Figure 3" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 3. </b><fig><p>Block diagram of a typical analog DLL.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/4808169/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div> The PD detects the phase difference between the reference signal <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-23-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-349" role="math" style="width: 2.902em; top: -2.298em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-350"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-351" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">(</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-352"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.502em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.152em 1000.75em 4.152em -999.998em); top: -3.998em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-353"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-354"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-355" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">V<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.202em;"></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.002em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.848em; left: 0.603em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-356"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-357"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-358" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">r</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-359" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">e</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-360" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">f<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.053em;"></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.002em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-361" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">)</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.302em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.372em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.378em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-45">{T}_{\rm clk}/{N}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. One of the main causes that degrades the performance of the DLL is the nonlinearity of the delay line. It causes the delay to deviate from the ideal value of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-46-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-611" role="math" style="width: 3.702em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.952em; height: 0px; font-size: 125%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.403em 1002.95em 2.702em -999.998em); top: -2.298em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-612"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-613"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.552em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.152em 1000.7em 4.152em -999.998em); top: -3.998em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-614"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-615"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-616" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">T<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.102em;"></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.002em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.848em; left: 0.603em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-617"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-618"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-619" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">c</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-620" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">l</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-621" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">k</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.002em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-622"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-623"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-624" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">/</span></span></span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-625"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-626"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-627" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">N<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.102em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.302em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.372em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.378em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-46">{T}_{\rm clk}/{N}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> due to the mismatch in the devices. Selecting a highly linear delay cell is an important criterion for the DLL to achieve accurate timing delay.
<div class="figure figure-full" id="fig4"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4808169/4808169-fig-4-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4808169/4808169-fig-4-small.gif" alt="Figure 4" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 4. </b><fig><p>Three operation conditions of the PD.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/4808169/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><div class="section_2" id="sec3a"><h3>A. Beam-Steering Architecture Using Partial DLL (P-DLL)</h3><p><a ref-type="table" anchor="table1" class="fulltext-link">Table I</a> shows the specifications of the true time-delay system or module for electronic beam steering. It provides multiple delayed reference clocks or signals for the array of PLLs or FSs. <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig5" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 5</a> shows the architecture of our IC design. It consists of a modified or P-DLL connected to a first set of multiplexer, digital phase interpolator (DPI) and a second set of multiplexers. Circuits for coarse and fine delay calibrations are crucial for compensating errors at the output. Finally, the delay outputs are buffered with slew-rate control.</p><p>
</p><div class="figure figure-full table" id="table1"><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Table I </b>Specifications of the Time-Delay Module for Beam Steering<div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></div><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4808169/4808169-table-1-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4808169/4808169-table-1-small.gif" alt="Table " /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div></div>
<div class="figure figure-full" id="fig5"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4808169/4808169-fig-5-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4808169/4808169-fig-5-small.gif" alt="Figure 5" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 5. </b><fig><p>Beam-steering IC architecture with true delay in picoseconds using modified DLL or P-DLL.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/4808169/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<div class="figure figure-full" id="fig6"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4808169/4808169-fig-6-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4808169/4808169-fig-6-small.gif" alt="Figure 6" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 6. </b><fig><p>Reference delay circuit schematic.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/4808169/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div> Our P-DLL incorporates two additional circuit blocks: a comparator at the input and a programmable reference delay before the PD block. The reference signal <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-47-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-628" role="math" style="width: 2.902em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.302em; height: 0px; font-size: 125%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.403em 1002.2em 2.702em -999.998em); top: -2.298em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-629"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-630" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">(</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-631"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.502em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.152em 1000.75em 4.152em -999.998em); top: -3.998em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-632"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-633"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-634" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">V<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.202em;"></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.002em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.848em; left: 0.603em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-635"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-636"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-637" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">r</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-638" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">e</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-639" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">f<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.053em;"></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.002em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-640" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">)</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.302em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.372em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.378em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-47">({V}_{\rm ref})</script></tex-math></inline-formula> can be derived from a crystal oscillator, up to a frequency of 100 MHz. The dc level for the comparator is set at 0.75 V. The comparator will convert the input signal to digital pulses <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-48-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-641" role="math" style="width: 2.002em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.602em; height: 0px; font-size: 125%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.453em 1001.6em 2.752em -999.998em); top: -2.298em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-642"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-643"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.602em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.152em 1000.75em 4.152em -999.998em); top: -3.998em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-644"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-645"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-646" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">V<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.202em;"></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.002em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.848em; left: 0.603em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-647"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-648"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-649" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">d</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-650" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">i</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-651" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">g</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.002em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.302em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.434em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.378em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-48">{V}_{\rm dig}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, which is operating at full swing if the signal amplitude is above 0.75 V. <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-49-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-652" role="math" style="width: 2.002em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.602em; height: 0px; font-size: 125%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.453em 1001.6em 2.752em -999.998em); top: -2.298em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-653"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-654"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.602em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.152em 1000.75em 4.152em -999.998em); top: -3.998em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-655"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-656"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-657" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">V<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.202em;"></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.002em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.848em; left: 0.603em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-658"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-659"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-660" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">d</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-661" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">i</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-662" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">g</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.002em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.302em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.434em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.378em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-49">{V}_{\rm dig}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is the input signal for the programmable reference delay, as well as the VCDL in this modified DLL.<p></p><p>The reference delay circuit can be programmed digitally using the “phase tuning control signal,” but this will initially introduces some delay error to this DLL. The idea here is to exploit the phase-locking mechanism of the DLL to lock or fix the relative time difference <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-50-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-663" role="math" style="width: 1.702em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.353em; height: 0px; font-size: 125%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.453em 1001.35em 2.603em -999.998em); top: -2.298em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-664"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-665"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.353em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.152em 1000.7em 4.152em -999.998em); top: -3.998em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-666"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-667"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-668" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">T<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.102em;"></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.002em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.848em; left: 0.603em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-669"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-670"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-671" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">r</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-672" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">d<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.002em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.302em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.247em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.191em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-50">{T}_{rd}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> or delay (<a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec3b" class="fulltext-link">Section III-B</a>) to give us a stable estimate of the delay first. This delay can be set from about 80, 85, to 500 ps and the typical measured error due to the reference delay circuit is about 20%. After determining the delay error (e.g., 20%) by measuring the output of the chip, we are able to correct this using our calibration circuits to give an accurate signal at the final output, as described in <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec3e" class="fulltext-link">Section III-E</a>. In general, additional delay errors due to mismatches in devices, etc., in the other part of the circuit will further contribute to the inaccuracy. Hence, calibration is required to give a well-controlled delay.</p><p>The 80–500-ps delay from this P-DLL can be further phase interpolated, as described in <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec3b" class="fulltext-link">Sections III-B</a> and <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec3d" class="fulltext-link">D</a> to give 5–75 ps. The multiplexers give various combinations of the signal to deliver from 0-, 5-, to 500-ps delay for beam steering. The measured results of our chip in <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec4" class="fulltext-link">Section IV</a> have validated our design methodology.</p></div><div class="section_2" id="sec3b"><h3>B. Reference Delay Circuit</h3><p>Our reference delay circuit consists of a chain of inverter buffers, as shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig6" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 6</a>. Each large delay buffer introduces about 500-ps delay, whereas the propagation delay of the small delay buffer is about 30 ps. The final delay is obtained by setting the binary code B0 to Bn through the “phase tuning control signal.” The PD compares the output of the VCDL with the delayed version of the reference signal <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-51-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-673" role="math" style="width: 1.702em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.353em; height: 0px; font-size: 125%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.453em 1001.35em 2.603em -999.998em); top: -2.298em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-674"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-675"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.353em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.152em 1000.75em 4.152em -999.998em); top: -3.998em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-676"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-677"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-678" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">V<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.202em;"></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.002em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.848em; left: 0.603em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-679"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-680"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-681" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">r</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-682" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">d<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.002em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.302em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.247em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.191em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-51">{V}_{rd}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. The P-DLL uses the inherent closed-loop mechanism to tune the VCDL and lock the time delay of the programmable reference delay circuit. In the locked condition, the delay of one unit of each voltage controlled delay cell is <disp-formula id="deqn5" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><div class="MathJax_Display"><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-52-Frame" tabindex="0" style="width: 100%;"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-683" role="math" style="width: 100%; display: inline-block; min-width: 8.253em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 100%; height: 0px; font-size: 125%; min-width: 8.253em;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(2.603em 1004.1em 4.902em -999.998em); top: -3.998em; left: 0.003em; width: 100%;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-684"><span class="mtable" id="MathJax-Span-685" style="min-width: 8.253em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 100%; height: 0px; min-width: 8.253em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: absolute; width: 4.103em; height: 0px; clip: rect(-1.397em 1004.1em 0.903em -999.998em); top: 0.003em; left: 50%; margin-left: -2.048em;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(2.603em 1004.1em 4.902em -999.998em); top: -3.998em; left: 0.003em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 4.103em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(2.502em 1004.1em 4.853em -999.998em); top: -3.897em; left: 50%; margin-left: -2.048em;"><span class="mtd" id="MathJax-Span-695"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-696"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-697"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.052em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.202em 1000.35em 4.152em -999.998em); top: -3.998em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-698" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">t</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.002em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.848em; left: 0.352em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-699"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-700"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-701" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">Δ</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.002em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-702" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.302em;">=</span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-703" style="padding-left: 0.302em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-704"><span class="mfrac" id="MathJax-Span-705"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.453em; height: 0px; margin-right: 0.102em; margin-left: 0.102em;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.152em 1001.35em 4.303em -999.998em); top: -4.697em; left: 50%; margin-left: -0.647em;"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-706"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.353em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.152em 1000.7em 4.152em -999.998em); top: -3.998em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-707" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">T<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.102em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.002em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.848em; left: 0.603em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-708"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-709"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-710" style="font-size: 70.7%; left: 0.603em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-740"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-741"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-742" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">d</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-743" style="font-size: 70.7%; Using a ten VCDL cell <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-57-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-745" role="math" style="width: 5.103em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 4.053em; height: 0px; font-size: 125%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.403em 1003.95em 2.702em -999.998em); top: -2.298em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-746"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-747" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">(</span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-748"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-749"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-750" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">N<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.102em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-751" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.302em;">=</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-752" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.302em;">10</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-753" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">)</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.302em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.372em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.378em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-57">({N}=10)</script></tex-math></inline-formula> in the P-DLL will lock the delay to 80 ps. If an additional 30-ps buffer is used, the delay is increased from about 80 to 83 ps. Hence, the theoretical delay resolution is about 3 ps, but in the actual design, we are able to achieve 5 ps with calibration. Hence, the actual calibrated output becomes 85 ps instead of 83 ps. Variations in process, supply voltage, and temperature produce a typical error of 20% delay in the reference delay circuit, but this can be measured and corrected later using calibrated circuits. Hence, the output of the P-DLL is 80, 85, and 90 ps up to 500 ps (using at least ten large buffers). We have to note that the various mismatches in the subsequent circuit blocks (multiplexers, etc.) will contribute further errors, which can be larger than the delay caused by the buffers of the reference delay circuit. Hence, our calibration circuits are crucial for correcting the errors generated from the P-DLL and the other part of the circuits to give the desired accurate delay.</p></div><div class="section_2" id="sec3c"><h3>C. Delay Cell</h3><p>The delay unit in the VCDL is a self-biased Maneatis loads differential delay cell, as used in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref4" id="context_ref_4_3c">[4]</a> and shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig7" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 7</a>. This delay cell has a high linearity range and power supply rejection ratio (PSRR) to ensure small timing jitter at the output. The effective delay of each cell is defined as <disp-formula id="deqn6" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><div class="MathJax_Display"><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-58-Frame" tabindex="0" style="width: 100%;"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-754" role="math" style="width: 100%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">F</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.002em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.302em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.247em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.191em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-60">C_{\rm EFF}</script></tex-math></inline-formula></td><td><p>effective delay cell output capacitance.</p></td></tr></tbody></table>
<div class="figure figure-full" id="fig7"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4808169/4808169-fig-7-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4808169/4808169-fig-7-small.gif" alt="Figure 7" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 7. </b><fig><p>Maneatis loads delay cell.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/4808169/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p>The delay <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-61-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-806" role="math" style="width: 1.353em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.052em; height: 0px; font-size: 125%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.502em 1001.05em 2.603em -999.998em); top: -2.298em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-807"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-808"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.052em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.202em 1000.35em 4.152em -999.998em); top: -3.998em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-809"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-810"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-811" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">t</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.002em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.848em; left: 0.352em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-812"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-813"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-814" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">Δ</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.002em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.302em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.247em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.128em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-61">{t}_{\Delta}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> of the variable delay cell unit dictates the true time delay generated through the P-DLL. The smallest delay is the minimum propagation delay of the delay cell when <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-62-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-815" role="math" style="width: 2.603em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.052em; height: 0px; font-size: 125%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.453em 1002.05em 2.603em -999.998em); top: -2.298em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-816"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-817"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.052em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.152em 1000.75em 4.152em -999.998em); top: -3.998em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-818"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-819"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-820" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">V<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.202em;"></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.002em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.848em; left: 0.603em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-821"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-822"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-823" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">t</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-824" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">u</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-825" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">n</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-826" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">e</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.002em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.302em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.247em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.191em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-62">{V}_{\rm tune}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is reaching its minimum level. The minimum delay time depends on the process technology. In this case, the chip has been implemented in lower cost 130-nm CMOS process, which gives a minimum delay of 80 ps after accounting for the variations in voltage, temperature, and process. The delay generated from this P-DLL is between 80–500 ps.</p></div><div class="section_2" id="sec3d"><h3>D. Phase Interpolation</h3><p>A secondary circuit has been implemented to achieve the time delay from 5 to 75 ps. The programmable time-delay operation is divided into two circuits, as shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig5" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 5</a>. The delay from 80 to 500 ps (ch1c–ch8c) at a 5-ps incremental step is generated through the P-DLL with the help of the small buffer in the programmable reference delay circuit. The DPI is introduced as a secondary circuit to cover the time delay from 5 to of 75 ps (ch1f–ch8f). The DPI is used to interpolate the rising edges of its two input signal. These inputs are connected to the outputs of two adjacent delay cells (ch1c and ch2c in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig5" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 5</a>) in the P-DLL through a multiplexer (Mux). The Mux will select from either the signals from the P-DLL or <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-63-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-827" role="math" style="width: 1.902em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.502em; height: 0px; font-size: 125%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.453em 1001.5em 2.603em -999.998em); top: -2.298em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-828"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-829"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.502em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.152em 1000.75em 4.152em -999.998em); top: -3.998em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-830"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-831"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-832" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">V<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.202em;"></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.002em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.848em; left: 0.603em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-833"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-834"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-835" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">r</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-836" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">e</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-837" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">f<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.053em;"></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.002em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.302em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.247em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.191em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-63">{V}_{\rm ref}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> as the input for the DPI. When the beam-steering system requires 0 ps or no delay, the Mux will select <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-64-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-838" role="math" style="width: 1.902em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.502em; height: 0px; font-size: 125%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.453em 1001.5em 2.603em -999.998em); top: -2.298em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-839"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-840"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.502em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.152em 1000.75em 4.152em -999.998em); top: -3.998em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-841"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-842"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-843" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">V<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.202em;"></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.002em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.848em; left: 0.603em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-844"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-845"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-846" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">r</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-847" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">e</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-848" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">f<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.053em;"></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.002em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.302em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.247em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.191em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-64">{V}_{\rm ref}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> as the input to the DPI.</p><p>The schematic of a short-circuit current suppression (SCCS) interpolator <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref17" id="context_ref_17_3d">[17]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref18" id="context_ref_18_3d">[18]</a> consisting of a pre-charge PMOS transistor and a pair of NMOS discharge transistors and logic circuits for the DPI is shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig8" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 8</a>. The SCCS interpolator is capable of producing a precise interpolation ratio. The interpolation error is minimized by suppressing the short-circuit current between <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-65-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-849" role="math" style="width: 2.353em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.852em; height: 0px; font-size: 125%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.453em 1001.85em 2.603em -999.998em); top: -2.298em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-850"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-851"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.852em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.152em 1000.75em 4.152em -999.998em); top: -3.998em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-852"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-853"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-854" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">V<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.202em;"></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.002em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.848em; left: 0.603em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-855"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-856"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-857" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">D</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-858" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">D</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.002em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.302em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.247em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.191em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-65">{V}_{DD}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and gnd during a period when both PMOS and NMOS transistors are switched on simultaneously. The interpolation circuit is a combination of two homo-interpolators and a hetero-interpolator, as shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig8" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 8(b)</a>. The homo-interpolator derives its inputs from the same signal source. The output from the homo-interpolator is the delayed input signal. The inherent delay <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-66-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-859" role="math" style="width: 2.952em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.353em; height: 0px; font-size: 125%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.453em 1002.35em 2.603em -999.998em); top: -2.298em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-860"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-861"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.353em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.152em 1000.7em 4.152em -999.998em); top: -3.998em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-862" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">T<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.102em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.002em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.848em; left: 0.603em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-863"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-864"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-865" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">h</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-866" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">o</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-867" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">m</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-868" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">o</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.002em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.302em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.247em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.191em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-66">T_{\rm homo}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> matches the propagation delay of a hetero-interpolator with inputs from two different signal sources for interpolation. The delay time for the interpolation circuit can be expressed as follows: <disp-formula id="deqn7-8" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><div class="MathJax_Display"><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-67-Frame" tabindex="0" style="width: 100%;"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-869" role="math" style="width: 100%; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.152em 1003.35em 4.303em -999.998em); top: -5.498em; right: 0.003em;"><span class="mtd" id="MathJax-Span-877"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-878"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-879"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.353em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.152em 1000.7em 4.152em -999.998em); top: -3.998em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-880" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">T<span style="display: inline-block;
