<div class="figure figure-full" id="fig8"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4808169/4808169-fig-8-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4808169/4808169-fig-8-small.gif" alt="Figure 8" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 8. </b><fig><p>DPI. (a) DPI circuit design. (b) Multiple DPI or D configuration and its characteristics.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/4808169/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p>The SCCS interpolator can achieve a precise interpolation ratio, as proven in <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn7-8" href="#deqn7-8" class="fulltext-link">(8)</a>. Each interpolator is able to halve the time difference between the rising edges of two input signals. There are four stages of interpolators connected in series inside the DPI block. The output time delay of the DPI block is <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-72-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1019" role="math" style="width: 3.202em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.552em; height: 0px; font-size: 125%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.403em 1002.5em 2.702em -999.998em); top: -2.298em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1020"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-1021"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.052em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.202em 1000.35em 4.152em -999.998em); top: -3.998em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1022"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1023"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1024" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">t</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.002em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.848em; left: 0.352em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1025"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1026"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1027" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">Δ</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.002em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1028"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1029"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-1030" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">/</span></span></span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-1031" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">16</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.302em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.372em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.378em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-72">{t}_{\Delta}/16</script></tex-math></inline-formula>; where <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-73-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1032" role="math" style="width: 1.353em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.052em; height: 0px; font-size: 125%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.502em 1001.05em 2.603em -999.998em); top: -2.298em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1033"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-1034"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.052em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.202em 1000.35em 4.152em -999.998em); top: -3.998em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1035"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1036"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1037" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">t</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.002em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.848em; left: 0.352em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1038"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1039"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1040" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">Δ</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.002em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.302em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.247em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.128em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-73">{t}_{\Delta}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is the time delay of ch1c and ch2c. When <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-74-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1041" role="math" style="width: 1.353em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.052em; height: 0px; font-size: 125%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.502em 1001.05em 2.603em -999.998em); top: -2.298em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1042"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-1043"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.052em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.202em 1000.35em 4.152em -999.998em); top: -3.998em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1044"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1045"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1046" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">t</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.002em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.848em; left: 0.352em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1047"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1048"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1049" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">Δ</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.002em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.302em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.247em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.128em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-74">{t}_{\Delta}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> of ch1c and ch2c is 80 ps, the relative delay at the DPI outputs is 5 ps. The DPI helps to reduce the delay (5–75 ps) beyond the limitation of the P-DLL.</p></div><div class="section_2" id="sec3e"><h3>E. Output Calibrations</h3><p>The programmable reference circuit, P-DLL, and mismatches due to transistors, layout, and bonding wires will contribute to the delay errors. This issue is even more critical when the delay is below sub-10 ps. Calibration circuits are required to compensate the errors due to the relative delay between the adjacent channels. Our calibration scheme consists of two sets of circuits to calibrate for each output or channel. The coarse calibrations for correcting the timing errors up to <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-75-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1050" role="math" style="width: 2.603em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.052em; height: 0px; font-size: 125%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.403em 1001.95em 2.702em -999.998em); top: -2.298em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1051"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-1052" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">+</span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1053"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1054"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-1055" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">/</span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-1056" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">−</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.302em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.372em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.378em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-75">+/-</script></tex-math></inline-formula>100 ps at a resolution of 10 ps and the fine calibrations for the timing errors up to <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-76-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1057" role="math" style="width: 2.603em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.052em; height: 0px; font-size: 125%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.403em 1001.95em 2.702em -999.998em); top: -2.298em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1058"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-1059" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">+</span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1060"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1061"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-1062" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">/</span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-1063" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">−</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.302em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.372em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.378em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-76">+/-</script></tex-math></inline-formula>10 ps at a resolution of 0.5 ps.</p><p>The calibration circuit consists of a series of binary weighted unit capacitor connected to each of the delayed output or channel. The value of the capacitive load connected to each delayed output is digitally programmed. <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig9" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 9(a)</a> shows one of the output channel connected to the capacitors for calibration, which we will refer to as “calibration capacitors.” Both coarse and fine calibration circuits are similar, except that the coarse calibration capacitors have a larger capacitance. When the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-77-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1064" role="math" style="width: 3.902em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 3.103em; height: 0px; font-size: 125%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.453em 1003.1em 2.603em -999.998em); top: -2.298em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1065"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-1066"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 3.103em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.152em 1002.75em 4.152em -999.998em); top: -3.998em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1067"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1068"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1069" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">C</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1070" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">T</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1071" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">R</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1072" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">L</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.002em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.848em; left: 2.802em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1073"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1074"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1075" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">i</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.002em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.302em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.247em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.191em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-77">{\rm CTRL}_{i}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> signal is “1,” the switch is connected to capacitor <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-78-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1076" role="math" style="width: 5.152em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 4.103em; height: 0px; font-size: 125%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.453em 1004.1em 2.603em -999.998em); top: -2.298em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1077"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-1078"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.052em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.152em 1000.75em 4.152em -999.998em); top: -3.998em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1079"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1080"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1081" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">C<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.053em;"></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.002em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.848em; left: 0.703em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1082"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1083"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1084" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">i</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.002em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-1085" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.202em;">+</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1086" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.202em;">Δ</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-1087"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.052em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.152em 1000.75em 4.152em -999.998em); top: -3.998em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1088"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1089"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1090" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">C<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.053em;"></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.002em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.848em; left: 0.703em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1091"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1092"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1093" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">i</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.002em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.302em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.247em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.191em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-78">{C}_{i}+\Delta{C}_{i}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>.</p><p>The calibration procedures are described as follows.
</p><ol><li><p>When the chip is first powered up, in the default state, all the channels will have their most significant bit (MSB) calibration bit (CTRLn) equal to “1” and the remaining bits <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-79-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1094" role="math" style="width: 11.753em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 9.402em; height: 0px; font-size: 125%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.403em 1009.3em 2.702em -999.998em); top: -2.298em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1095"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-1096" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">(</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-1097"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 3.252em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.152em 1002.75em 4.152em -999.998em); top: -3.998em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1098"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1099"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1100" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">C</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1101" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">T</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1102" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">R</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1103" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">L</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.002em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.848em; left: 2.802em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1104"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1105"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-1106" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">0</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.002em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-1107" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.202em;">−</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-1108" style="padding-left: 0.202em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 4.202em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.152em 1002.75em 4.152em -999.998em); top: -3.998em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1109"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1110"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1111" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">C</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1112" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">T</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1113" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">R</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1114" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">L</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.002em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.848em; left: 2.802em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1115"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1116"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1117"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1118"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1119" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">n</span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-1120" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">−</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-1121" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">1</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.002em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-1122" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">)</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.302em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.372em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.378em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-79">({\rm CTRL}_{0}-{\rm CTRL}_{{n}-1})</script></tex-math></inline-formula> equal to “0.” All the channels are loaded with half of the total “calibration capacitors.”</p></li><li><p>Once the desired delay is programmed using the “phase tuning control signal,” the relative delay between the signals from the adjacent output channels is monitored using an oscilloscope.</p></li><li><p>If the error is larger than <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-80-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1123" role="math" style="width: 2.603em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.052em; height: 0px; font-size: 125%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.403em 1001.95em 2.702em -999.998em); top: -2.298em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1124"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-1125" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">+</span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1126"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1127"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-1128" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">/</span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-1129" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">−</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.302em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.372em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.378em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-80">+/-</script></tex-math></inline-formula>10 ps, the delay is calibrated using a series of coarse “calibration capacitors.” The number of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-81-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1130" role="math" style="width: 3.902em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 3.103em; height: 0px; font-size: 125%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.453em 1003.1em 2.603em -999.998em); top: -2.298em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1131"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-1132"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 3.103em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; width: 0px; height: 4.002em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.848em; left: 2.802em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1139"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1140"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1141" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">i</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.002em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.302em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.247em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.191em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-81">{\rm CTRL}_{i}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> bits to be switched either on (“1”) or off (“0”) will depend on the value of the errors and whether the error is positive (relative delay is too large) or negative (relative delay is too small).</p></li><li><p>When the measured error is less than <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-82-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1142" role="math" style="width: 2.603em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.052em; height: 0px; font-size: 125%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.403em 1001.95em 2.702em -999.998em); top: -2.298em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1143"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-1144" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">+</span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1145"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1146"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-1147" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">/</span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-1148" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">−</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.302em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.372em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.378em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-82">+/-</script></tex-math></inline-formula>10 ps, the fine “calibration capacitors” are used to minimize the error to within <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-83-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1149" role="math" style="width: 2.603em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.052em; height: 0px; font-size: 125%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.403em 1001.95em 2.702em -999.998em); top: -2.298em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1150"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-1151" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">+</span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1152"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1153"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-1154" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">/</span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-1155" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">−</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.302em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.372em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.378em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-83">+/-</script></tex-math></inline-formula>0.5 ps. A similar procedure of programming the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-84-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1156" role="math" style="width: 3.902em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 3.103em; height: 0px; font-size: 125%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.453em 1003.1em 2.603em -999.998em); top: -2.298em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1157"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-1158"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 3.103em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.152em 1002.75em 4.152em -999.998em); top: -3.998em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1159"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1160"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1161" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">C</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1162" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">T</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1163" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">R</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1164" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">L</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.002em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.848em; left: 2.802em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1165"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1166"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1167" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">i</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.002em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.302em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.247em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.191em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-84">{\rm CTRL}_{i}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> bits is also carried out for the process of fine calibration.</p></li><li><p>If the error is <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-85-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1168" role="math" style="width: 3.952em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 3.152em; height: 0px; font-size: 125%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.403em 1003.05em 2.702em -999.998em); top: -2.298em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1169"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-1170" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">&lt;</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-1171" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.302em;">+</span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1172"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1173"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-1174" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">/</span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-1175" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">−</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; (b) Single bit relative capacitance. (c) Simulated relative delay between channel 1 and channel 2 when the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-86-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1176" role="math" style="width: 4.103em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.052em; height: 0px; font-size: 125%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.403em 1001.95em 2.702em -999.998em); Each delayed output or channel has its own set of calibration circuit that can be calibrated independently. The fine and coarse calibrations are implemented using the concept of “relative delay” <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref6" id="context_ref_6_3e">[6]</a> with the schematics shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig9" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 9(a)</a>. As shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig9" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 9(b)</a>, there are two branches of capacitors for each control bit <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-88-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1195" role="math" style="width: 4.902em; The switches and the inter-connections contribute to the capacitance of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-89-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1209" role="math" style="width: 1.353em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.052em; height: 0px; font-size: 125%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.453em 1001.05em 2.603em -999.998em); top: -2.298em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1210"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-1211"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.052em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.152em 1000.75em 4.152em -999.998em); top: -3.998em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1212"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1213"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1214" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">C<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.053em;"></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.002em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.848em; left: 0.703em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1215"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1216"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1217" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">i</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.002em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.302em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.247em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.191em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-89">{C}_{i}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> of both branches. The <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-90-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1218" role="math" style="width: 1.353em; If <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-92-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1236" role="math" style="width: 4.103em; This will also change the relative delay between two channels because the time difference is proportional to <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-95-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1279" role="math" style="width: 2.502em; vertical-align: -0.247em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.191em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-95">\Delta{C}_{1}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. vertical-align: -0.247em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.191em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-96">\Delta{C}_{1}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> consists of both NMOS <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-97-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1299" role="math" style="width: 3.103em; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.102em;"></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.002em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.848em; This has the following advantages. Firstly, using the relative capacitances can eliminate the effect of parasitic capacitances from the switches and metal inter-connections to achieve the fine or small delay. Secondly, this design is easy to implement since it only needs a switch to select either of the two capacitances. Thirdly, the area of the layout will be smaller if <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-99-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1321" role="math" style="width: 2.002em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.602em; height: 0px; font-size: 125%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.453em 1001.6em 2.452em -999.998em); top: -2.298em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1322"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1323" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Δ</span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1324"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1325"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1326" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">C<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.053em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.302em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.059em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.066em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-99">\Delta{C}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> was generated using metal layers. <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig9" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 9(c)</a> shows the simulated results of the delay between channels 1 and 2 using our fine calibrations. Channel 2 least significant bit (LSB) calibration bit (i.e., <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-100-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1327" role="math" style="width: 7.153em; The relative delay between these channels is about 250 fs at a typical corner simulation. The worst case corner simulation shows that the delay is about 0.5 ps. left: 0.953em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1388"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1389"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1390" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">P<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.102em;"></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.002em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.302em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.247em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.191em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-104">{W}_{P}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>.<p></p><p>The delayed outputs from the P-DLL (ch1c–ch8c) and DPI (ch1f–ch8f) are connected to a multiplexer. Depending on the requirement of beam steering, either P-DLL or DPI will be selected as the outputs. The eight true time-delayed outputs from the multiplexer are connected to a set of slew-rate controlled buffers. The circuit is designed to drive high impedance and 50-<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-105-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1391" role="math" style="width: 0.903em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.703em; height: 0px; font-size: 125%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.453em 1000.65em 2.452em -999.998em); top: -2.298em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1392"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1393" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Ω</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.302em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.059em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.003em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-105">\Omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula> loads (but not simultaneously).</p></div></div>
<div class="section" id="sec4"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION IV.</div><h2>Results</h2></div><div class="section_2" id="sec4a"><h3>A. Beam-Steering Device Measurements</h3><p>Our IC has been implemented using a 130-nm CMOS process operating at 1.5 V. The microphotograph of the chip is shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig10" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 10</a>. <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig11" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 11</a> shows the measurement setup with the chip mounted on the printed circuit board (PCB) for testing purposes.</p><p>
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig10"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4808169/4808169-fig-10-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4808169/4808169-fig-10-small.gif" alt="Figure 10" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 10. </b><fig><p>IC die photograph.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/4808169/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<div class="figure figure-full" id="fig11"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4808169/4808169-fig-11-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4808169/4808169-fig-11-small.gif" alt="Figure 11" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 11. </b><fig><p>Setup for measuring true time-delay IC module.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/4808169/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig12" class="fulltext-link">Figs. 12</a> and <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig13" class="fulltext-link">13</a> show the measured results of the chips operating at the delay of 5 and 500 ps, respectively. The oscilloscope can only measure up to four channels at one time, but similar results are also observed in the remaining four ports of the chip. <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig12" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 12</a> indicates that the time difference between channels 1 and 2 is 5.03 ps, channels 1 and 3 is 10. 39 ps, and channels 1 and 4 is 15.57 ps. Hence, the relative time delay is between ports and is close to 5 ps. The measured results have validated the calibration accuracy and is well within 0.5 ps.<p></p><p>
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig12"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4808169/4808169-fig-12-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4808169/4808169-fig-12-small.gif" alt="Figure 12" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 12. </b><fig><p>Measured time-delay outputs of the chip at 5 ps.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/4808169/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<div class="figure figure-full" id="fig13"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4808169/4808169-fig-13-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4808169/4808169-fig-13-small.gif" alt="Figure 13" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 13. </b><fig><p>Measured time-delay outputs of the chip at 500 ps.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/4808169/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<div class="figure figure-full table" id="table2"><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Table II </b>Summary of the Measured Results of the IC Chip<div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></div><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4808169/4808169-table-2-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4808169/4808169-table-2-small.gif" alt="Table " /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div></div> The measured jitter for 5-ps time delay are 2 ps [root mean square (rms)] and 18 ps (peak to peak), respectively. The measured results are summarized in <a ref-type="table" anchor="table2" class="fulltext-link">Table II</a>. The active die size excluding bond pads is 1.2 <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-106-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1394" role="math" style="width: 2.652em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.103em; height: 0px; font-size: 125%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.302em 1002.1em 2.452em -999.998em); top: -2.298em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1395"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-1396"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.103em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.402em 1001.65em 4.152em -999.998em); top: -3.998em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1397"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1398"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-1399"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1400"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-1401" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">mm</span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.002em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -4.348em; left: 1.652em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1402"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1403"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-1404" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">2</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.002em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.302em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.059em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.191em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-106">{\hbox{mm}}^{2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. Power consumption is about 10 mA, much lower than DDS, which consumes several hundreds milliamperes.<p></p></div><div class="section_2" id="sec4b"><h3>B. Radiation Patterns and RFID Reader Protocol Testing</h3><p>Our beam-steering module was tested with different sets of transmitter arrays at 900-MHz and 2.4-GHz bands. We have designed an RFID interrogator with one receiver, but two sets of transmitters and FS, which can operate from 902 to 928 MHz according to ISO 18000-6B protocol <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref5" id="context_ref_5_4b">[5]</a>. The beam-steering module feeds two synthesizers, each with 10-MHz reference signals. These can be time shifted or delayed according to control settings for the IC. The FSs can hop at 500-kHz channels with a Manchester coded amplitude shift-keying signal across 902–928 MHz, but the radiation pattern measurements were performed using a continuous wave fixed at 924 MHz. For this experiment, an array of two dipole antennas spaced at about a half-wavelength (16.23 cm) was connected to outputs of two transmitters only. Using a time delay at 0, 22, and 44 ps would translate to a phase difference of 0°, 7.318°, and 14.64° according to <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn3" href="#deqn3" class="fulltext-link">(3)</a>. The corresponding scanned angle of the phased array would change from 0°, 2.32° and 4.65° respectively, as shown in <a ref-type="table" anchor="table3" class="fulltext-link">Table III</a>, using <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn2" href="#deqn2" class="fulltext-link">(2)</a>. Generally, the main lobe scanned or steered as the time delay increased, as shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig14" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 14</a>. There were good agreements at bore-sight (0°) with 0-ps delay and scanned angle of 2° using 22-ps delay, but there was some discrepancy
</p><div class="figure figure-full table" id="table3"><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Table III </b>Scanned Angle Versus Time Delay (Phase Difference) for the Phased Arrays at Two Frequencies<div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></div><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4808169/4808169-table-3-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4808169/4808169-table-3-small.gif" alt="Table " /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div></div>
<div class="figure figure-full" id="fig14"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4808169/4808169-fig-14-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4808169/4808169-fig-14-small.gif" alt="Figure 14" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 14. </b><fig><p>Measured radiation patterns at 924 MHz using array of 2 antennas.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/4808169/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<div class="figure figure-full" id="fig15"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4808169/4808169-fig-15-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4808169/4808169-fig-15-small.gif" alt="Figure 15" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 15. </b><fig><p>Measured radiation patterns at 2.412 GHz using an array of four antennas.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/4808169/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div> between the theoretical and measured scanned angle at 44-ps delay. The ripples observed in the pattern have created some distortions in the measured results. This problem has occurred because of the difficulty in synchronizing the transmitters of the phased array with the remote receiver setup at 924 MHz. However, there was no problem synchronizing at 2.412 GHz, as shown by the radiation patterns in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig15" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 15</a>. In this case, our beam-steering chip was tested using four sets of commercial RF transceivers obtained from MAXIM, for IEEE 802.11g/802.11b. In this experiment, the adjacent antenna spacing was spaced 3.7 cm apart to give an antenna aperture length of 11.1 cm for four linearly polarized discone antennas. The phased array was also scanned at similar angles as 924 MHz, but the time delay required for 2.412 GHz is 5 and 10 ps, respectively, much smaller than 22 and 44 ps for 924 MHz. This is to be expected since the higher carrier frequency translates to a shorter cycle. A smaller time-delay step is required to achieve the same scanned accuracy. Very good agreements between theoretical and measured results were also observed in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig15" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 15</a> and <a ref-type="table" anchor="table3" class="fulltext-link">Table III</a> at 2.412 GHz.<p></p><p>Finally, the chip was further validated in an RFID interrogator operating at ISO 18000-6b protocols at 900-MHz band using the same setup as <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref5" id="context_ref_5_4b">[5]</a>. In this experiment, the performance of a single antenna, beam-switching, and electronic beam-scanning using two transmitters and one receiver was compared. Note that in a modulated backscattering RFID system, the backscattering tag does not used an RF reference oscillator so there is no need to synchronize with the transceiver of the RFID reader, unlike the remote receiver setup used for pattern measurements (<a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig14" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 14</a>). Here, the experimental setup was meant to emulate a typical indoor environment for item level tagging. An array of two circular polarized antenna connected to a reader were located at 1.2 m above the floor. There were 48 commercial RFID tags (each the size of a credit card) mounted on a fabric. The tags are packed less than 2 mm apart and arranged side-by-side into two vertical columns and 24 horizontal rows <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref5" id="context_ref_5_4b">[5]</a>. Our beam-steering module was able to scan the phased array up to 22-ps time-delay resolution to give the 2° scanned angle. The carrier frequencies was hopping from 900 to 928 MHz according to the ISO-180006b communication protocols. The poorest performance was obtained using a single antenna where only 21% of the tags were read by the reader. However, better results were obtained using our beam-scanning method with a 78% success rate. Beam switching achieved only a 35% success rate. Such performances were also observed at further distance from the tags. Similar measured results were also reported using the commercial DDS from Analog Devices <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref5" id="context_ref_5_4b">[5]</a>. The beam-steering array using our chip has helped to power up more passive tags to improve the RFID system performance, which uses the ISO-180006b protocol. Better read rates may be improved by redesigning the tags or changing the position of the tags, but this is not always possible in practice.</p><p>Practical testing of a wireless communication link using our transmit beam-steering array at 2.4 GHz will require measuring the performance of bit error rate (BER) and packet error rate (PER) of several remote active receivers or tags under various propagation channel conditions, i.e., receivers located at different positions in the room, corridor, etc., over a wide area. This will require launching a dedicated test and measurement campaign using communication protocols analyzers, testers, etc. Several earlier works, such as <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref3" id="context_ref_3_4b">[3]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref19" id="context_ref_19_4b">[19]</a>, and <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref20" id="context_ref_20_4b">[20]</a>, have proven that transmit beam steering can improve the performance of WLANs with their measured and simulated results. Thus, our study will complement these results by providing a low-cost IC chip solution.</p></div></div>
<div class="section" id="sec5"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION V.</div><h2>Conclusion</h2></div><p>A low-power CMOS IC based on a new P-DLL architecture can provides up to 5-ps delay resolution for beam scanning has been developed for multiband and multimode RFID applications. The chip can enable the RF FSs in the transmitter chains of a phased array to reconfigure the beams adaptively. The measured radiation patterns for phased arrays at 900 MHz and 2.4 GHz have been validated. The chip has also improved the system performance of an RFID interrogator and passive tags operating in the ISO 18000-6b standard.</p></div>
<h3>ACKNOWLEDGMENT</h3><p>The authors would like to acknowledge the support of A*STAR, Singapore, and N. Cahoon, IBM, Boston, MA, in the business partner program.</p></div></div>

<script>

function getCookie(name) {
	var nameEQ = name + "=";
	var ca = document.cookie.split(';');
	for(var i=0;i &lt; ca.length;i++) {
		var c = ca[i];
		while (c.charAt(0)==' ') c = c.substring(1,c.length);
		if (c.indexOf(nameEQ) == 0) return c.substring(nameEQ.length,c.length);
	}
	return null;
}

j$('document').ready(function(){
	if(getCookie('legacyUserName')!=null)
	{
		if(IBP_WS_ENABLED_FLAG){
		Modal.refreshLegacyAccountTransition('/xpl/mwLegacyAccountTransition.jsp');
		}
	}
});

</script>

In this paper, a novel and low-power CMOS chip has been designed to enable beam steering for the RFID interrogator. This is suitable for the RFID system, operating from 900-MHz to 2.4-GHz bands, which uses passive and active RF tags. Our solution does not change the basic transceiver design in order to minimize the cost of the system. The chip has been implemented in 130-nm CMOS. It can provide up to eight time shifted signals to feed the multiple RF synthesizers in a phased array. This is suitable for the RFID reader, which requires multibands and multimodes, covering ISO-18000-6, Electronic Product Code, and IEEE 802.11b/g standards. The size of this die is 1.2 mm&lt;sup&gt;2&lt;/sup&gt; and it consumes only 10 mA. It can provide multiple delayed signals with 5-ps resolution. This will translate to a 2deg scanned angle at 2.4-GHz band. Measured results for the integrated circuit and phased arrays will be
